< review>
Good place for what it is. If you buy lots of vegies and fruits, you can save about 75%  on equally fresh produce to major supermarket. The veriety of imported specialty foods also makes this place a good choice for the frugal, the cultured, and the budget shopper. They are not "Saks or Neiman's" people. We are so used to that phony friendliness in retail that we lose sight of value and availability of rare products this place offers. $9 for cherries at Ralph's comes with a fake smile.< /review>

<UserId.>102330294009146773607< /UserId.><text>This is my go-to place for all kinds of ethnic foods from Asia, Africa and Europe. Among the interesting stuff one can score here are a few types of phyllo pastry (Greece and Turkey) , many kinds of buckwheat and canned fish and mushrooms (Russia, Estonia, Poland), all sorts of Middle Eastern produce and prepared foods, freshly baked breads and a slew of exotic dairy products such as Ryazhenka, Lebni and Kashkaval.
Hands down the best choice of Feta cheese both local and imported.
Produce is OK but not great although there are items that you won't normally find in other stores like for example bulgur and some rare fresh herbs. Butcher has cold and hot smoked mackerel from Norway, which are one of my favorite dinners with some potato salad. Decent quality lamb and goat cuts for curries and North African specialties  and you can find all the spices needed for that as well. <Time>1532981455377< /Time><pics>None</pics><Review>KC Plumbing and the Hydroflow miracle product.
I run An American Car Wash in Palm Desert opposite Whole Foods. We had two major issues: We need spot-free water and we needed to kill all the germs in our newly installed reclaimed water system so there would be no health risk or smell. We wash 8,000-10,000 cars a month. It takes 41,000 gallons of water to do this, but we are now able to reclaim 60% of this water. The fresh water from the CVWD has lots of calcium and other minerals that will spot your car (leave your car by a sprinkler and see what happens). Left untreated, reclaim water has bacteria in it and therefore can have an unpleasant smell and potentially bad germs so we had Kelly and Casey from KC Plumbing install their Hydroflow system. Installation was fast and efficient and the product is amazing. 1) The water is now spot free, so there is no risk of water spots if a car is left to dry in the sun, which is great for our express customers. 2) No servicing is required, no adding salt, nothing‚Ä¶ it just runs. 3) Our valves and tubes are no longer clogged with calcium or other minerals. 4) There is no more odor from our reclaim water and all the bacteria is destroyed. 5) The best part is that the payback compared to a less effective soft water system (resin and salt) is only one year. Yes it will pay itself back in one year for us and do more to boot.  I can highly recommend KC plumbing and the Hydroflow system. If it works for us it should work for anyone. I will be putting one in my home pool and we are fitting them now to our mobile car wash steam machines.<//Review><username>David Kartal<//username><gmap_id>0x80db1c9477e5414b:0x85a95db9c1fb0383<//gmap_id><rate>5<//rate>< UserId.>

<response>None< /response><Rating>2< /Rating><Time>1347224018731</Time><review>DON'T USE KC'S 23 1/2 HOUR PLUMBING UNLESS YOU WANT TO PAY THREE TIMES WHAT A NORMAL COMPANY WOULD CHARGE!

I found KC's in the Yellow Pages. On 7/13/12 I called to arrange an emergency repair. Robert Martinez from KC's Plumbing arrived to estimate the job at 9AM to repair a leaking 3/4" copper tee. I had already dug a pit to provide access to the tee for repair.

Unfortunately he wasn't able shut off the water completely to perform the repair so he would have to replace the ball valve by the meter. He also recommended installing a pressure regulator at the meter as well.

His three estimates of "about" $400 for each of the three repairs totaled $1,200 plus $59 service call. He said the "about" $400 was to protect him if the actual costs were higher. I asked him if the job actually cost less would he charge yes. His reply was "Absolutely".

I am the caretaker here for a 5 acre property in Sky Valley. The Veterinarian that owns the property was the person responsible for the bill so I introduced him to Robert so he could approved the repairs.

I arrange all contractors performing services on the property and normally supervise the entire job. In this case however, I had a prior medical appointment so I could not be there for the entire job.

Upon my return from the doctor at 12 Noon Robert was gone. I assumed he had just taken a lunch break since the pit that I dug for the repair was left open. I looked in the pit and saw that the tee valve was repaired so I assumed the ball valve and pressure regulator were installed. Strange that he wouldn't fill up the hole that I had dug for him

I then had to dig up the area around the water meter to inspect the ball valve and regulator installation. I asked the homeowner if Robert had showed him the completed work. He had not. All he did was go to the main house to get a check for the full $1,259. So much for the "Absolutely he would adjust the bill accordingly if the work cost less".

I did some research and a pressure regulator is $150 at Home Depot and a ball valve is $15, plus the copper tee and some solder so let's say $200 for parts and materials.

That leaves $1,059 charged for labor. I did some checking and even emergency weekend or after hour calls to plumbers ran $150/hr at the most. This was not the weekend nor after hours. The top hourly charge for normal calls is around $100.

I contacted KC's to complain about the charges and the owner, Mr Russum, told me that they always include a new ball valve when they install a pressure regulator and didn't know why Robert double charged. Said he must have been having a bad day. Anyway, Mr. Russum credited $400 so the bill was now $859. I asked him so why was I charge $659 labor for 3 hours work?

He said he would have Robert call me to try to straighten it out.. When he called I had him speak with the homeowner and he said, "It's like when you go in for car repairs and sign an estimate approving the charges." He got upset when we told him that was a ridiculous analogy and hung up accusing of us of recording his conversation. I should have. If I would have told him that I was going to record the call I'm sure he wouldn't have gone on an on trying to justify his outrageous repair charges.

So I was feeling generous and said OK, $3 hours at $100 per hour is $300. I contacted the owner again requested an additional discount of $300 for the excess labor charges. He said, "Now this is getting out of hand." Subsequent emails with detailed pictures of the sloppy job and the dirty work area and uncovered pit left by Mr. Martinez went unanswered.

PS To add insult to injury I had to fill the hole and clean up his mess myself. So much for their advertising claim, "Customer Satisfaction Guaranteed."<//review>< Gmap_id>
